in the validation schema. This affects fields recursively,\n    69→\t// but switches back to normal pruning behaviour if nested\n    70→\t// properties or additionalProperties are specified in the schema.\n    71→\t// False means that the pruning behaviour is inherited from the parent.\n    72→\t// False does not mean to activate pruning.\n    73→\tXPreserveUnknownFields bool\n    74→\n    75→\t// x-kubernetes-embedded-resource defines that the value is an\n    76→\t// embedded Kubernetes runtime.Object, with TypeMeta and\n    77→\t// ObjectMeta. This extension\n   111→\t//      may be used on any type of list (struct, scalar, ...).\n   112→\t// 2) `set`:\n   113→\t//      Sets are lists that must not have multiple items with the same value. Each\n   114→\t//      value must be a scalar (or another atomic type).\n   115→\t// 3) `map`:\n   116→\t//      These lists are like maps in that their elements have a non-index key\n   117→\t//      used to identify them. Order is preserved upon merge. The map tag\n   118→\t//      must only be used on a list with elements of type object.\n   119→\tXListType *string\n   120→\n   121→\t// x-kubernetes-map-type annotates an object to further describe its topology.\n   122→\t// This extension must only be used when type is object and may have 2 possible values:\n   123→\t//\n   124→\t// 1) `granular`:\n   125→\t//      These maps are actual maps (key-value pairs) and each fields are independent\n   126→\t//      from each other (they can each be manipulated by separate actors).    *int64\n   155→\tPattern          string\n   156→\tMaxItems         *int64\n   157→\tMinItems         *int64\n   158→\tUniqueItems      bool\n   159→\tMultipleOf       *float64\n   160→\tEnum annotation states\ntype APIApprovalState int\n\nconst (\n\t// APIApprovalInvalid means the annotation doesn't have an expected value\n\tAPIApprovalInvalid APIApprovalState = iota\n\t// APIApproved if apiextensionsv1.KubeAPIApprovedAnnotation)\n\tcase strings.HasPrefix(annotation, \"unapproved\"):\n\t\treturn APIApprovalBypassed, fmt.Sprintf(\"not approved: %q\", annotation)\n\tcase schema publishing chain in kubernetes/kubernetes follows this path:\\n\\n**1. CRD Validation Schema Definition (Source)**\\n\\nThe validation schema originates in the CustomResourceDefinition API type (staging/src/k8s.io/apiextensions-apiserver/pkg/apis/apiextensions/types.go). Each CRD version specifies a validation schema via the CustomResourceValidation struct, which contains an OpenAPIV3Schema field of type JSONSchemaProps. The JSONSchemaProps type (types_jsonschema.go) defines the actual JSON Schema properties including type, format, validation constraints, and Kubernetes-specific extensions like x-kubernetes-preserve-unknown-fields and x-kubernetes-int-or-string.\\n\\n**2. Structural Schema Extraction**\\n\\nThe conversion pipeline begins in the OpenAPI controller (staging/src/k8s.io/apiextensions-apiserver/pkg/controller/openapi/builder/builder.go) with the generateBuilder function. It retrieves the validation schema for a specific CRD version using GetSchemaForVersion (apihelpers/helpers.go), which accesses crd.Spec.Versions[version].Schema. The JSONSchemaProps is then converted to an internal structural schema representation via NewStructural (apiserver/schema/convert.go). This function validates that the schema is structurally sound by checking for unsupported fields and recursively converting the schema hierarchy. The Structural type (apiserver/schema/structural.go) represents a schema that separates structural information (type, properties, items, additionalProperties) from value validation rules (format, minimum, maximum, etc.).\\n\\n**3. Schema Validation and Processing**\\n\\nThe structural schema undergoes validation using ValidateStructural (apiserver/schema/validation.go) to ensure it meets Kubernetes structural invariants. The schema may be unfolded (expanding nested validations) and have value validations stripped depending on the OpenAPI version target (v2 vs v3).\\n\\n**4. OpenAPI Schema Conversion**\\n\\nThe Structural schema is converted to OpenAPI format via the ToKubeOpenAPI() method (apiserver/schema/kubeopenapi.go). This method recursively traverses the Structural schema and converts it to go-openapi spec.Schema objects, mapping structural properties to OpenAPI properties, handling items, additionalProperties, and converting Kubernetes extensions (x-kubernetes-*) to OpenAPI vendor extensions.\\n\\n**5. Full OpenAPI Spec Generation**\\n\\nThe BuildOpenAPIV2 and BuildOpenAPIV3 functions (controller/openapi/builder/builder.go) create complete OpenAPI specifications from the CRD. These functions generate REST API routes (GET, POST, PUT, DELETE, PATCH operations), configure the converted schema, and use kube-openapi builders to generate the final spec document. For v2, specs may be further converted to remove unsupported features via ToStructuralOpenAPIV2 (controller/openapi/v2/conversion.go).\\n\\n**6. OpenAPI Spec Merging**\\n\\nThe generated CRD specs are merged with other CRD specs for the same API group/version using MergeSpecs (v2) or MergeSpecsV3 (v3) functions (controller/openapi/builder/merge.go). These functions combine multiple CRD specs while preventing conflicts.\\n\\n**7. API Server Publication**\\n\\nThe OpenAPI controllers (staging/src/k8s.io/apiextensions-apiserver/pkg/controller/openapi/controller.go for v2 and pkg/controller/openapiv3/controller.go for v3) watch CustomResourceDefinition resources and trigger spec generation whenever a CRD is created or updated. The controllers call BuildOpenAPIV2/BuildOpenAPIV3 and then publish the merged specs via openAPIService.UpdateGroupVersion() or openAPIV3Service.UpdateGroupVersion(). These services make the specs available through the API server's /openapi/v2 and /openapi/v3 endpoints, allowing clients to discover the schema and API structure of custom resources.\\n\\n**Key architectural points:** The CustomResourceValidation.OpenAPIV3Schema is the source of truth for the schema. The Structural intermediate representation serves as an abstraction that separates structural properties from validation rules, enabling flexible conversion to different OpenAPI versions. schema publishing chain in kubernetes/kubernetes follows this path:\\n\\n**1. CRD Validation Schema Definition (Source)**\\n\\nThe validation schema originates in the CustomResourceDefinition API type (staging/src/k8s.io/apiextensions-apiserver/pkg/apis/apiextensions/types.go). Each CRD version specifies a validation schema via the CustomResourceValidation struct, which contains an OpenAPIV3Schema field of type JSONSchemaProps. The JSONSchemaProps type (types_jsonschema.go) defines the actual JSON Schema properties including type, format, validation constraints, and Kubernetes-specific extensions like x-kubernetes-preserve-unknown-fields and x-kubernetes-int-or-string.\\n\\n**2. Structural Schema Extraction**\\n\\nThe conversion pipeline begins in the OpenAPI controller (staging/src/k8s.io/apiextensions-apiserver/pkg/controller/openapi/builder/builder.go) with the generateBuilder function. It retrieves the validation schema for a specific CRD version using GetSchemaForVersion (apihelpers/helpers.go), which accesses crd.Spec.Versions[version].Schema. The JSONSchemaProps is then converted to an internal structural schema representation via NewStructural (apiserver/schema/convert.go). This function validates that the schema is structurally sound by checking for unsupported fields and recursively converting the schema hierarchy. The Structural type (apiserver/schema/structural.go) represents a schema that separates structural information (type, properties, items, additionalProperties) from value validation rules (format, minimum, maximum, etc.).\\n\\n**3. Schema Validation and Processing**\\n\\nThe structural schema undergoes validation using ValidateStructural (apiserver/schema/validation.go) to ensure it meets Kubernetes structural invariants. The schema may be unfolded (expanding nested validations) and have value validations stripped depending on the OpenAPI version target (v2 vs v3).\\n\\n**4. OpenAPI Schema Conversion**\\n\\nThe Structural schema is converted to OpenAPI format via the ToKubeOpenAPI() method (apiserver/schema/kubeopenapi.go). This method recursively traverses the Structural schema and converts it to go-openapi spec.Schema objects, mapping structural properties to OpenAPI properties, handling items, additionalProperties, and converting Kubernetes extensions (x-kubernetes-*) to OpenAPI vendor extensions.\\n\\n**5. Full OpenAPI Spec Generation**\\n\\nThe BuildOpenAPIV2 and BuildOpenAPIV3 functions (controller/openapi/builder/builder.go) create complete OpenAPI specifications from the CRD. These functions generate REST API routes (GET, POST, PUT, DELETE, PATCH operations), configure the converted schema, and use kube-openapi builders to generate the final spec document. For v2, specs may be further converted to remove unsupported features via ToStructuralOpenAPIV2 (controller/openapi/v2/conversion.go).\\n\\n**6. OpenAPI Spec Merging**\\n\\nThe generated CRD specs are merged with other CRD specs for the same API group/version using MergeSpecs (v2) or MergeSpecsV3 (v3) functions (controller/openapi/builder/merge.go). These functions combine multiple CRD specs while preventing conflicts.\\n\\n**7. API Server Publication**\\n\\nThe OpenAPI controllers (staging/src/k8s.io/apiextensions-apiserver/pkg/controller/openapi/controller.go for v2 and pkg/controller/openapiv3/controller.go for v3) watch CustomResourceDefinition resources and trigger spec generation whenever a CRD is created or updated. The controllers call BuildOpenAPIV2/BuildOpenAPIV3 and then publish the merged specs via openAPIService.UpdateGroupVersion() or openAPIV3Service.UpdateGroupVersion(). These services make the specs available through the API server's /openapi/v2 and /openapi/v3 endpoints, allowing clients to discover the schema and API structure of custom resources.\\n\\n**Key architectural points:** The CustomResourceValidation.OpenAPIV3Schema is the source of truth for the schema. The Structural intermediate representation serves as an abstraction that separates structural properties from validation rules, enabling flexible conversion to different OpenAPI versions. The controller pattern ensures specs are kept up-to-date whenever CRDs change, and the publishing layer makes these specifications available to API clients and tools.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
